[<p>Most great stock pickers do all they can to preserve their competitive edge. David Webb is trying to make his disappear.</p>, <p>The former Barclays banker isn't opposed to making money per se. After earning about 20 per cent a year from his personal investments in Hong Kong shares since 1995 \u2013 more than double the gains in the city's benchmark index - he seems happy to have amassed a fortune of at least $US170 million ($245 million).</p>, <p>David Webb is pushing for reform. <cite><span class="ojLwA">Credit:</span>Bloomberg</cite></p>, <p>But Webb finds the source of his outperformance troubling. In his view, beating Hong Kong's stock market by such a wide margin has only been possible because of the city's weak corporate governance and lax regulatory oversight.</p>, <p>While Hong Kong ranks favourably in international surveys of corruption and the ease of doing business, a spate of corporate scandals and wild small-cap stock swings have rocked the city's equity market in recent years. The benchmark Hang Seng Index is valued at less than 10 times its companies' reported earnings, one of the lowest levels worldwide.</p>, <p>"Think of me as an expert mechanic, walking around a second-hand car lot in which there are no warranties, and all of them are discounted for the risk of being lemons,'' Webb explained in a recent speech at The University of Hong Kong. By avoiding most of the lemons most of the time "and getting a substantial discount on good companies, I have been able to outperform.''</p>, <p>Webb's no-frills site is required reading for Hong Kong investors.<cite><span class="ojLwA">Credit:</span>Bloomberg</cite></p>, <p>Webb wants to help the investing public steer clear of Hong Kong's lemons, too. Over the past 20 months, he has advised readers of his widely followed website to avoid more than 75 of the city's publicly traded companies -- several of which subsequently became targets of the largest-ever raid by Hong Kong's securities regulator. Stocks on his "not to own'' lists have lost $US16 billion of their value since he warned against buying them.</p>, <p>Webb said he doesn't profit from any of this work, which takes up about half his time. Now 53 and comfortably rich, he's OK with giving away his research -- even if doing so ends his run as one of the world's best stock pickers.</p>, <p>"I don't want to reach the end of my life and say, 'I was a really good investor, that was fun, but I didn't advance the human condition,''' he said in an interview at his home office in Hong Kong's Mid-Levels district, where he works until 2 a.m. most nights poring through financial statements and other corporate disclosures.</p>, <p>His attempts to clean up Hong Kong's stock market trace back to 1998, when he decided to quit working life at age 33 to manage his own money. Most of his reform efforts since then have revolved around Webb-site.com, a forum for his views on regulation, corporate developments, and other market news. The ad-free site is required reading in Hong Kong investing circles, despite a layout that hasn't changed since the dial-up age (Webb's kids have lobbied for an update, to no avail).</p>, <p>Webb, who was sent by Barclays to Hong Kong from London in 1991, has also pushed for change behind the scenes. By his own tally, he has sent more than 1,000 letters to Hong Kong Exchanges &amp; Clearing Ltd. and the Securities and Futures Commission on topics ranging from company disclosure lapses to trading rules. When he served as an independent director of Hong Kong's stock exchange operator from 2003 to 2008, board meetings lasted at least an hour longer than usual, said Oscar Wong, a former director who sat next to Webb at the monthly gatherings.</p>, <p>"He would pry into every aspect of the exchange,'' Wong said, adding that he generally supported Webb's positions. "He raised a lot of topics of public interest.''</p>, <p>Webb spends hours poring over financial statements of Hong Kong companies.<cite><span class="ojLwA">Credit:</span>Shutterstock</cite></p>, <p>Spokesmen for the SFC and HKEX declined to comment on Webb.</p>, <p>Webb has his fair share of detractors. He has often been too quick to dismiss the viewpoints of Hong Kong's local brokerage community, said Choi Chen Po-sum, a vice chairman of the Hong Kong stock exchange in the 1990s who's now chairman of National Resources Securities Ltd. An ultimately successful campaign to end stock trading-fee minimums in the mid 2000s spurred some in the local press to label him an agent of foreign hedge funds, an allegation he laughs off.</p>, <p>There is something more to life than just making money,</p>, <p>Yet even his critics admit that Webb's an unusually astute investor. His publicly disclosed stock holdings - which likely understate his total wealth - have swelled to about $US170 million from $US30 million in 2003, when Hong Kong's exchange started publishing the data.</p>, <p>Webb estimates his annualised gains since 1995 at about 20 per cent, versus an 8.4 per cent total return for the Hang Seng Index. While he declined a Bloomberg News request to view his trading records, Hong Kong market veterans including CMB International Securities Ltd. strategist Daniel So and Accudo Capital Ltd. Chief Executive Officer Manuel Schlabbers have said that his stated returns are plausible.</p>, <p>Here's how Webb describes the basics of his investment strategy:</p>, <p>The reports on companies to avoid are a byproduct of his stock-picking process. "I am looking for good companies, but when you do that, you find an awful lot of rubbish," he said. "Things like the Enigma Network pop out."</p>, <p>That's the name Webb coined for the group of 50 Hong Kong companies he told investors "not to own" in May 2017. Six weeks after he alleged that the stocks were entwined in a complex web of cross-shareholdings that had pushed their valuations to unsustainable levels, 38 of them plunged suddenly, some by more than 90 per cent.</p>, <p>Webb estimates his annualised gains since 1995 at about 20 per cent, versus an 8.4 per cent total return for the Hang Seng Index.<cite><span class="ojLwA">Credit:</span>AP</cite></p>, <p>Hong Kong law enforcement officials and the SFC have since conducted 20 search operations, seized more than 4,000 items of evidence and arrested at least three senior executives with ties to the companies, according to a person familiar with matter who asked not to be named because the details aren't public. The SFC is preparing to file charges this year.</p>, <p>The prescience of the Enigma Network warning has only increased Webb's influence. In October, his research on companies linked to China Huarong Asset Management Co., a scandal-plagued bad-loan manager, sent several stocks tumbling by about 10 per cent. In mid-November, he triggered a $US228 million selloff after highlighting shares at risk of trading suspensions because of what he called a misguided Hong Kong stock exchange proposal to change its listing rules.</p>, <p>While Webb doubts that Hong Kong will reform its markets any time soon, he says the benefits would be enormous: higher equity valuations, more public companies and a lower cost of capital for businesses across the economy. His portfolio would also get a one-time boost as Hong Kong's lemon discount disappeared. Finding mispriced stocks would become much harder afterward, but Webb could live with that.</p>, <p>"There is something more to life than just making money,'' he said.</p>, <p><strong>Bloomberg</strong></p>, <p>Copyright \xa9 <!-- -->2019</p>]

[<p class="">A company that owns two national for-profit college chains said Thursday that it will erase nearly $500 million in debt incurred by former students as part of a settlement with 48 states and the District of Columbia.</p>, <p class="">The deal with Career Education Corporation will resolve allegations that it lied about job placement rates and misled potential students to get them to enroll. State attorneys general began investigating the company in 2014 following complaints from students and a damning report by the U.S. Senate.</p>, <p class="">Company officials on Thursday said they deny any wrongdoing but called the settlement an "important milestone."</p>, <p class="">"We have remained steadfast in our belief that we can work with the attorneys general to demonstrate the quality of our institutions and our commitment to students," Todd Nelson, the company's CEO, said in a statement.</p>, <p class="">Based in Schaumburg, Illinois, the company enrolls about 34,000 students across two chains, Colorado Technical University and American InterContinental University. More than 90 percent of its students are enrolled through online courses, according to the company.</p>, <p class="">The deal was signed by every state except California, which is negotiating a separate agreement of its own, and New York, which previously settled with the company.</p>, <p class="">Of the $493 million in debt being wiped out, the greatest share comes from borrowers in Florida, which will get $68 million in relief, followed by Texas, with $51 million. The debt stems from institutional loans the company issued to students.</p>, <p class="">Other terms of the deal require the company to pay $5 million to states to cover the cost of their investigations, and the company will now be required to give all prospective students a single-page disclosure with information including job placement rates, anticipated costs and the average earnings of graduates.</p>, <p class="">State attorneys general called the agreement a victory for students, saying it will provide debt relief to more than 179,000 borrowers across the country. In Illinois, where $48 million will be cleared, Attorney General Lisa Madigan said it's a fair outcome for students who were deceived by the company's schools.</p>, <p class="">"Today's settlement ensures the company treats students the way they should have been all along \u2014 with honesty and respect for their futures," Madigan said.</p>, <p class="">At its peak, Career Education Corporation ranked among the largest for-profit college companies in the nation, enrolling more than 100,000 students at several chains including Sanford-Brown College and Le Cordon Bleu, a group of culinary schools.</p>, <p class="">But after years of government scrutiny and deep enrollment declines, the company announced in 2015 it would begin closing or selling most of its schools.</p>, <p class="">Aside from the state investigations, the company has also been the subject of a Federal Trade Commission inquiry since 2015, according to company records filed in September with the U.S. Securities and Exchange Commission. The FTC has been examining potential deception in advertising, according to the company, which says it is cooperating with the inquiry.</p>, <p class="">The for-profit college industry faced a heavy crackdown under President Barack Obama but has seen <a href="https://www.nbcnews.com/news/education/profit-colleges-struggle-despite-assist-betsy-devos-n863641" target="_blank">a shift in its favor </a> under President Donald Trump. Over the last two years, Education Secretary Betsy DeVos has sought to loosen regulation and reverse policies created under the previous administration.</p>, <p class="lastMarkupItem">But the sector has come under renewed scrutiny in recent weeks following the <a href="https://www.nbcnews.com/news/education/major-profit-college-chain-abruptly-announces-closure-dozens-schools-n944696" target="_blank">abrupt closure</a> of Education Corporation of America, which was one of the nation's largest chains before it <a href="https://www.nbcnews.com/news/us-news/students-stunned-after-major-profit-college-chain-closes-they-re-n944976" target="_blank">collapsed amid deep financial trouble</a>. Democrats have cited the closure as evidence that the industry needs sharper oversight.</p>, <p class="copyright___3CuB7 founders-mono f2 lh-none ls-tight">\xa9 <!-- -->2019<!-- --> NBC UNIVERSAL</p>]

[<p>Firm used Dutch shell company in move known as \u2018double Irish, Dutch sandwich\u2019 that cuts its foreign tax bill</p>, <p class="byline" data-component="meta-byline" data-link-name="byline">Reuters</p>, <p aria-hidden="true" class="content__dateline">\n<time class="content__dateline-wpd js-wpd" data-timestamp="1546555280000" datetime="2019-01-03T17:41:20-0500" itemprop="datePublished">\nThu 3 Jan 2019 <span class="content__dateline-time">17.41\xa0EST</span>\n</time>\n<time class="content__dateline-lm js-lm u-h" data-timestamp="1546558948000" datetime="2019-01-03T18:42:28-0500" itemprop="dateModified">\nLast modified on Thu 3 Jan 2019 <span class="content__dateline-time">18.42\xa0EST</span>\n</time>\n</p>, <p>Google moved \u20ac19.9bn ($22.7bn) through a Dutch shell company to <a class="u-underline" data-component="auto-linked-tag" data-link-name="auto-linked-tag" href="https://www.theguardian.com/world/bermuda">Bermuda</a> in 2017, as part of an arrangement that allows it to reduce its foreign tax bill, according to documents filed at the Dutch chamber of commerce.</p>, <p>The amount channelled through Google <a class="u-underline" data-component="auto-linked-tag" data-link-name="auto-linked-tag" href="https://www.theguardian.com/world/netherlands">Netherlands</a> Holdings BV was about \u20ac4bn more than in 2016, the documents, filed on 21 December, showed.</p>, <p>\u201cWe pay all of the taxes due and comply with the tax laws in every country we operate in around the world,\u201d <a class="u-underline" data-component="auto-linked-tag" data-link-name="auto-linked-tag" href="https://www.theguardian.com/technology/google">Google</a> said in a statement.</p>, <p>\u201cGoogle, like other multinational companies, pays the vast majority of its corporate income tax in its home country, and we have paid a global effective tax rate of 26% over the last 10 years.\u201d</p>, <p>For more than a decade the arrangement has allowed Google\u2019s owner, <a class="u-underline" data-component="auto-linked-tag" data-link-name="auto-linked-tag" href="https://www.theguardian.com/technology/alphabet">Alphabet</a>, to enjoy an effective tax rate in the single digits on its non-US profits, about a quarter of the average tax rate in its overseas markets.</p>, <p>The subsidiary in the Netherlands is used to shift revenue from royalties earned outside the US to Google Ireland Holdings, an affiliate based in Bermuda, where companies pay no income tax.</p>, <p>The tax strategy, known as the \u201cdouble Irish, Dutch sandwich\u201d, is legal and allows <a class="u-underline" data-link-name="in body link" href="https://www.theguardian.com/technology/2018/jan/24/google-ceo-were-happy-to-pay-more-tax">Google</a> to avoid triggering US income taxes or European withholding taxes on the funds, which represent the bulk of its overseas profits.</p>, <p>However, under pressure from the European Union and the United States, Ireland in 2014 decided to phase out the arrangement, ending Google\u2019s tax advantages in 2020.</p>, <p>Google Netherlands Holdings BV paid \u20ac3.4m in taxes in the Netherlands in 2017, the documents showed, on a gross profit of \u20ac13.6m.</p>]

[<p><strong><b>Summary</b></strong></p>, <p>Biomedical refrigerators and freezers are medical equipment, used for storing various biological samples such as biological reagents, blood, blood derivatives, medicines, vaccines, deoxyribonucleic acid (DNA), ribonucleic acid (RNA), and flammable chemicals. Samples with biological origin require precise conditions for effective storage. In comparison with domestic refrigerators and freezers, biomedical refrigerators and freezers provide optimum conditions for efficient storage of samples with biological origin.</p>, <p><strong><b>Download Research Study With Latest Advancement Trends and Application</b></strong><strong><b>\xa0@</b></strong><b> </b><strong><b>\xa0</b></strong><a href="https://www.reportsmonitor.com/request_sample/273363"><strong><u><b>https://www.reportsmonitor.com/request_sample/273363</b></u></strong></a></p>, <p>Key factors driving the growth include the growing prevalence of chronic diseases, rising demand for storing biological products, blood samples, blood reagents, vaccines, DNA samples and other chemicals. In addition, the need to provide thermal insulation and avoid product degradation is a critical factor boosting the usage rates. Factors like the increasing emphasis on energy efficient refrigerators impelling the prospects for market growth until the end of the forecast period. The environmental challenge for biomedical refrigerator and freezer manufacturers has always been to minimize energy consumption. According to the current standards, refrigerants used have an ozone depleting potential of zero, minimum global warming potential and be non-toxic as well as inflammable. It is tough to meet all these requirements while maintaining a stable temperature control. Therefore, manufacturers are looking for technologies to maximize efficiency and temperature uniformity while minimizing heat and energy consumption.</p>, <p>North America accounts for the largest share of the global biomedical refrigerators and freezers market, and is expected to dominate the market in the forecast period. However, Asia-Pacific is expected to be the fastest growing region for the biomedical refrigerators and freezers market. [<p>In response to tightened regulation over shoppers who buy luxury products overseas on behalf of Chinese mainland customers, the buyers - "<em>daigou</em>" in Chinese pinyin - are coming up with increasingly creative ways of promoting their business, like posting crude sketches on WeChat as advertising or using memes to disguise their activities and evade tax. <br/><br/></p>, <p style="font-size: 13px; font-family: verdana; font-weight: bold; margin-top: 3px">Sellers promote cosmetics with their drawings on WeChat. Source: The Paper</p>, <p><br/><br/>"This lipstick is very beautiful. I have two. Baby, do you need one? Only 155 rmb ($ 23)," posted a <em>daigou</em> along with a crude colored drawing the lipstick.<br/><br/><br/><br/></p>, <p style="font-size: 13px; font-family: verdana; font-weight: bold; margin-top: 3px">A Seller promotes a MAC lipstick with crude drawings on WeChat. Source: The Paper </p>, <p><br/><br/>Some <em>daigou</em> summarized their linguistic skills in posts along with a simple drawing of a product in a not-too-subtle disguise for a product advertisement. <br/><br/></p>, <p style="font-size: 13px; font-family: verdana; font-weight: bold; margin-top: 3px">A Seller promotes a MAC lipstick with crude drawings on WeChat. Source: The Paper</p>, <p><br/><br/>"You could use your face to illuminate the entire room during a power outage. I have a light bulb that is just reserved for you, making your face brighter than the light bulb," a <em>daigou</em> cryptically told customer in a post that was an introduction the\xa0Japanese cosmetic SK-II, according to a report in the Paper.\xa0 <br/><br/></p>, <p style="font-size: 13px; font-family: verdana; font-weight: bold; margin-top: 3px">"I want to introduce Lu Han's younger sister, Luna to all of you," said a seller's post. Source: The Paper </p>, <p><br/><br/>"If I use actual photos of my products in my WeChat advertising, their logos will be recognized by algorithms designed by relevant government agencies. Source: The Paper </p>, <p>China's first e-commerce law, which became effective on Tuesday, requires vendors on e-commerce platforms, WeChat, live-streaming websites and other online platforms to register as a business, obtain a license, pay required taxes and be held responsible for selling fake goods. Rule-breakers can face fines up to 2 million yuan ($290,900).</p>]

[<p>The economy has become heavily dependent on financial asset prices. Thus, the recent volatility in the stock and bond markets bear close watching.</p>, <p>These price swings are likely to persist, especially if the Federal Reserve makes a policy mistake. This probability is rising, as Fed members are effectively trying to engineer a soft landing, i.e., a cyclical downturn that avoids a recession, in both the financial markets and the real economy. This is something that has never happened before.</p>, <p>At present, the level of total financial assets as a share of GDP is at a record high. This is troubling and no doubt related in large part to extraordinary monetary policy actions taken during and after the financial crisis.</p>, <p>The Fed implemented zero interest rates, quantitative easing and forward guidance to stimulate the economy. Surging financial asset values were part of the calculus.</p>, <p>In turn, the ratio of financial assets to GDP stood at 4.35 in the third quarter (3Q) of 2018, the last quarter for which official data are available. This was up from 4.31 in Q2 2018 and is up markedly from the last business cycle\u2019s peak of 3.80 in Q3 2007.</p>, <p>A chart from 2002 to 2018 shows exponential growth in this ratio. However, the series looks like it has reached its apex.</p>, <p>According to our calculations, the ratio of financial assets to GDP fell last quarter to 4.29. This would be the first decline since Q2 2016 and the largest decline since Q3 2015. The Fed releases the official Q4 2018 data on March 7.\xa0</p>, <p>With the Fed on path to raise rates further this year (and next) and with the balance sheet on track to shrink by approximately $600 billion in 2019 alone, the value of financial assets is likely to decline further. Monetary policy was much looser in 2015 and 2016, which allowed financial markets to recover.</p>, <p>Importantly, the ratio of financial assets to GDP peaked before the onset of each of the last two recessions. Hence, we wonder whether we are on the cusp of another such decline, with obvious negative economic implications to follow. Why is the Fed not more concerned?</p>, <p>Outside of autos and housing, the economic fundamentals still look good: The unemployment rate is at a five-decade low and real GDP appears to be relatively robust. However, too much of past Fed behavior was geared toward stimulating financial markets.</p>, <p>Given their massive size, the Fed faces a dilemma albeit of\xa0its own making. Tighten too much and the economy will rollover. Tighten too little\xa0and the financial asset share of GDP potentially scales new heights. The central issue then becomes, how best to proceed?</p>, <p>Let the economy run hot, and keep interest rates low in order to stimulate a sustained cyclical lift in inflation. While financial markets could then potentially reheat, a Fed engineered recession would be even worse. Monetary policymaking needs a do-over and soon. We hope the central bank is listening.</p>, <p style="font-weight: 400;"><em>Joseph LaVorgna is the chief economist for the Americas at Natixis, an\xa0international corporate and investment banking, asset management, insurance and financial services arm of Groupe BPCE, the 2nd-largest banking group in France with 31.2 million clients spread over two retail banking networks, Banque Populaire and Caisse d\u2019Epargne.</em></p>, <p><a href="http://thehill-v4.disqus.com/?url=https%3A%2F%2Fthehill.com%2Fopinion%2Ffinance%2F423561-market-volatility-has-the-fed-facing-a-dilemma-of-its-own-making">View the discussion thread.</a></p>, <p>The Hill 1625 K Street, NW Suite 900 Washington DC 20006 | 202-628-8500 tel | 202-628-8503 fax</p>, <p>The contents of this site are \xa92019 Capitol Hill Publishing Corp., a subsidiary of News Communications, Inc.</p>]
[<p>By\xa0<a class="ca-a-md ca-a-blk" href="#author-information" rel="author"><span itemprop="name">Mark Huffman</span></a></p>, <p dir="ltr"><img alt="Photo" class="large aligncenter" data-id="45526" src="https://media.consumeraffairs.com/files/cache/news/Recession_and_finance_concept_claffra_Getty_Images_large.jpg" style="undefined">Apple stunned Wall Street Wednesday when it issued first quarter guidance that was sharply lower than what investors expected.</img></p>, <p dir="ltr">The tech giant reduced its estimates of revenue based on a number of economic factors, including the trade war with China and a stronger dollar. And it turns out Apple may not be alone in having to deal with less-than-expected revenue.</p>, <p dir="ltr">New data released Wednesday show U.S. manufacturing slowed considerably in December. The U.S. Purchasing Managers Index (PMI), compiled by IHS Markit, fell to 53.8 last month, down nearly two points from November.</p>, <p dir="ltr">Not only was it the index\u2019s lowest number over the last 15 months, it showed job creation had slowed to an 18-month low. A strong labor market, with near-record low unemployment, has been a major factor in propelling the U.S. economy.</p>, <p dir="ltr">"Output and order books grew at the lowest rates for over a year and optimism about the outlook slumped to its gloomiest for over two years," Chris Williamson, Markit's chief business economist <a href="https://www.cnbc.com/2019/01/02/december-manufacturing-pmi-shows-economic-trouble.html">told CNBC</a>. "Some of the weakness is due to capacity constraints, with producers again reporting widespread difficulties in finding suitable staff and sourcing sufficient quantities of inputs."</p>, <p dir="ltr">The issue of tariffs imposed against U.S. trading partners appears to be having a negative impact. Williamson said there are signs of slowing demand, along with concerns over the tariffs. Two-thirds of manufacturers are attributing higher costs to the tariffs.</p>, <p dir="ltr">Optimism, which was sky-high 12 months ago, has fallen. Manufacturers\u2019 confidence in their business has fallen to the lowest level in two years. In particular, manufacturers are concerned about how long the growth in new business will last.</p>, <p dir="ltr">Apple applied more gloom to the manufacturing situation when it warned investors that it doesn\u2019t expect to earn as much revenue from iPhone sales as previously forecast. It blamed the drop in sales on trade tensions with China, noting that sales to the country have been sharply lower. Other analysts, however, pointed out that iPhones selling for around $1,000 are having to compete with much cheaper Android devices.</p>, <p dir="ltr">Apple lowered revenue guidance to $84 billion, down from the nearly $93 billion it had previously forecasted. The futures prices now show a nearly 90% probability that interest rates will be at their current level or lower by the end of 2019. That is a 180-degree reversal from just several months ago when investors were betting on a 90% probability of higher rates. </p> <p> That expectation has been prompted by headwinds facing the global economy, including weak manufacturing data coming out of China and a contraction in global trade driven by the US trade war. </p> <p> European stocks were mixed following a selloff in Asian equities, led by China. [<p>Come January, many people will vow to eat healthier or get in shape. But, honestly, New Year's resolutions be damned, because guys, <a class="" href="https://people.com/food/girl-scout-cookie-season-start-date-january-new-cookie/" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">Girl Scout cookie season has officially started</a> and what's life without a few boxes of Thin Mints, right?</p>, <p>Although the holiday season might be over, there's no need to get into a funk. When one door closes, another door opens \u2014\xa0and that door, my friends, leads to Girl Scout cookies. On Wednesday, Girl Scouts all across the nation got the go-ahead to start selling cookies, according to <em>People,</em> which means people will be able to get their sweet treat fix in no time.</p>, <p>And you definitely don't want to miss out on this year's selection; 2019 marks the<a class="" href="https://www.usatoday.com/story/money/2019/01/02/girl-scout-cookies-return-new-year-caramel-chocolate-chip/2450440002/" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank"> debut of a new cookie</a>, Caramel Chocolate Chip, according to <em>USA Today</em>, which is just as delightful as it sounds. The cookie is gluten free <em>and</em> has a "hint of sea salt," which is perfect for lovers of sweet and savory foods. This is pretty special considering it's been two years since a new cookie was debuted, according to <em>USA Today, </em>so the wait is definitely worth it. </p>, <p>See? 2019 is already bringing good things. </p>, <p>And of course,<a class="" href="https://abcnews.go.com/GMA/Food/girl-scouts-share-taste-caramel-chocolate-chip-cookie/story?id=59929402" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank"> the classic cookies</a> are still going to be available, according to ABC News. So, people can still get their Thin Mint, shortbread (or Trefoil), and Caramel deLite (or Samoa) fix \u2014 and able to stock up on <a class="" href="https://www.girlscouts.org/en/cookies/all-about-cookies/Meet-the-Cookies.html" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">their favorite Girl Scout cookie</a> that they missed throughout the summer and holiday season. </p>, <p>Girl Scout cookie season <a class="" href="https://www.elitedaily.com/p/how-long-are-girl-scout-cookies-available-buy-some-boxes-while-you-can-7844687" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">only lasts until April</a> \u2014 which is plenty of time for people to enjoy their favorite cookies or restock on their favorites after underestimating how many cookies they'd eat. But since it has been nine months since you could last buy them, it's understandable why some would want to get their cookies <em>now</em>.</p>, <p>Thankfully, there are a few ways for people to get their Girl Scout cookie fix, even if they don't know any Girl Scouts themselves. All you have to do is<a class="" href="https://www.girlscouts.org/en/cookies/cookies.html?#27607" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank"> enter in your zip code on the Girl Scout's</a> website, and it will tell you exactly where (and when) a local troop will be selling cookies in your area throughout the next few months. If you're more of a mobile person, there is also a Girl Scout Cookie Finder app for phones that will show you where you need to go. </p>, <p>Aside from the obvious reasons, buying Girl Scout cookies does more than make you (and the people in your home) happy. Purchasing a box of Girl Scout cookies <a class="" href="https://www.girlscouts.org/en/cookies/all-about-cookies/support-girls-success.html?utm_campaign=CookieFY19&amp;utm_medium=Social_Council&amp;utm_source=5Skills_Twitter" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">allows young girls to succeed </a>and shows them that people care about their success. This helps in building the next generation of female entrepreneurs, according to <em>USA Today</em>, since the cookie program is the "largest girl-led entrepreneurial program in the world," according to the Girl Scout Association. Not to mention, the profits made during the sale stay local, allowing the troops to experience new opportunities.</p>, <p>So, purchasing a box of cookies will not only support your sweet tooth but will support dozens of young girls as well and show them that they can do anything. </p>, <p><b><em>After a very frustrating first birth experience, this Deaf mother wanted a change. Will the help of two Deaf doulas give the quality communication and birth experience this mom wants and deserves? Watch Episode Four of Romper's </em>Doula Diaries, Season Two<em>, below, and visit </em><a class="" href="https://www.youtube.com/user/EliteDaily" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank"><em>Bustle Digital Group's YouTube page</em></a><em> for more episodes.</em></b></p>]
[<p>Front page layout</p>, <p>Site theme</p>, <p>Sign up or login to join the discussions!</p>, <p class="byline" itemprop="author creator" itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">\n<a href="https://arstechnica.com/author/megan-geuss/" itemprop="url" rel="author"><span itemprop="name">Megan Geuss</span></a>\n    -  <time class="date" data-time="1546560627" datetime="2019-01-04T00:10:27+00:00">Jan 4, 2019 12:10 am UTC</time>\n</p>, <p>According to the Fraunhofer Institute, Germany's renewable power sector produced more electricity than coal in 2018 for the first time ever, with renewables providing 40 percent of the year's produced electricity and <a href="https://www.reuters.com/article/us-germany-power-renewables/renewables-overtake-coal-as-germanys-main-energy-source-idUSKCN1OX0U2">coal providing 38 percent</a>.</p>, <p>Of course, "renewables" include an aggregate of different sources\u2014solar, wind, hydroelectric, and biomass\u2014while coal is just a single fuel source (renewable energy has not yet displaced all fossil fuel use in Germany, you'll note). But coal has long been a staple of the country's energy mix, and Germany looks poised to <a href="https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2018-11-30/germany-closes-last-coal-mine-despite-decades-of-supplies-needed">reduce the amount of coal-fired power</a> on its grid significantly, even shutting down its last coal mine in November. From now on, coal for the approximately 120 coal-fired power plants that still power the German grid will be imported from the US, Russia, or Colombia, <a href="https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2018-11-30/germany-closes-last-coal-mine-despite-decades-of-supplies-needed">according to Bloomberg</a>.</p>, <p>The massive year for renewables was led by continued expansion in the wind energy sector. German <a href="https://www.spglobal.com/platts/en/market-insights/latest-news/electric-power/010319-german-wind-power-output-soars-to-new-annnual-record-on-december-surge">wind power output was up 5.4 percent year over year</a>, and output is expected to increase again in 2019. Alone, wind contributed to covering 19 percent of Germany's 2018 electricity demand, the largest source second only to lignite coal.</p>, <p>Reuters notes that critics are claiming favorable weather patterns, rather than sustainable growth, helped the country produce more renewable energy this year than last year. Indeed, a prolonged sunny summer increased solar output, but the hot year also reduced hydroelectric output considerably. Germany added 3.2 gigawatts (GW) of solar to an existing 45.5 GW last year.</p>, <p>The remainder of Germany's 2018 electricity production came from gas plants and nuclear plants. The country is hoping to phase out nuclear energy by 2022.</p>, <p>Germany has made considerable strides to <a href="https://arstechnica.com/information-technology/2017/07/germanys-power-sector-making-serious-strides-in-renewable-energy/">add renewable energy to its electricity sector</a>, but as in most countries, heating and transportation are the most difficult sectors of the economy to decarbonize. Germany introduced the world's first <a href="https://arstechnica.com/science/2018/09/first-hydrogen-powered-train-hits-the-tracks-in-germany/">hydrogen-powered train</a> earlier this year, but electric vehicles still only make up a small percentage of the country's vehicles. November, however, saw electric vehicle registrations <a href="https://insideevs.com/electric-car-sales-germany-new-high-in-november-2018/">account for nearly 2 percent of all registrations</a>.</p>, <p>Germany is Europe's largest economy, but it's not the only country showing healthy renewable numbers. Early last year, Portugal was able to produce more renewable electricity than total electricity demanded for the whole month of March, and the country had <a href="https://arstechnica.com/tech-policy/2018/04/portugal-set-some-big-renewable-energy-records-in-march/">several near-three-day stretches</a> when electricity demand was only met by renewable electricity. In addition, the UK has had <a href="https://arstechnica.com/science/2017/04/uk-first-coal-free-power-day/">coal-free days since 2017</a> and is reducing its coal reliance significantly.</p>, <p id="reply">You must <a class="vote_login" href="https://arstechnica.com/civis/ucp.php?mode=login&amp;return_to/science/2019/01/renewables-led-by-wind-provided-more-power-than-coal-in-germany-in-2018/">login or create an account</a> to comment.</p>, <p>Join the Ars Orbital Transmission mailing list to get weekly updates delivered to your inbox.</p>, <p id="copyright-terms">\n  CNMN Collection<br/>\n  WIRED Media Group<br/>\n  \xa9 2019 Cond\xe9 Nast. [<p>SALEM, Ohio \u2014 Although they\u2019d rather have free trade and market access, farmers say the $12 billion in commodity assistance being offered by President Donald Trump is worth applying for, in a year of high yields and low prices.</p>, <p>Known as the <a href="https://www.farmers.gov/manage/mfp" onclick="javascript:_gaq.push(['_trackEvent','outbound-article','http://www.farmers.gov']);">Market Facilitation Program</a>, the program compensates farmers who grew various crops \u2014 including corn, soybeans and wheat, and for livestock, including dairy \u2014 for price losses due to the trade war of 2018, and retaliatory tariffs that China enacted on U.S. farm goods.</p>, <p>Farmers can receive $1.65 per bushel of soybeans, 14 cents per bushel of wheat, 1 cent per bushel of corn, 12 cents per 100 pounds of milk, and $8 per head of hogs. Sorghum, almonds, cotton and cherries are also included, and the program also sets aside funds for developing new foreign markets, and purchasing more than two dozen select products, including fresh fruits and vegetables, nuts, meat and dairy.</p>, <p>The deadline to apply is Jan. 15, and the deadline to certify production is May 1. There is a cap of $125,000 per producer, for livestock claims, and the same amount for crop claims.</p>, <p>But even with the help, farmers question whether it will be enough to cover their losses, and for how long.</p>, <p>\u201cIt\u2019s really not even going to come close to making up for the damage that the market has experienced,\u201d said John Torres, director of government and industry affairs for the Ohio Corn and Wheat Growers Association.</p>, <p>\u201cWhat\u2019s going to be most beneficial to farmers is resuming national trade,\u201d he said.</p>, <p>Ron Elliott, a dairy and crop farmer from Knox County, said that assistance \u201cdoes help,\u201d but that the program is basically a way of compensating for the market potential that the government disrupted.</p>, <p>\u201cI\u2019d much rather get my income from the marketplace,\u201d he said.</p>, <p>Elliott and his brother, Bob, milk about 130 head on a farm that\u2019s been in the family since the early 1800s. He said farmers will have to do some paperwork, but that depending on the size of their operation and what they grow, \u201cit\u2019s going to be worth the effort.\u201d</p>, <p>In November, the U.S. and China agreed to a 90-day truce over their trade dispute, halting new tariffs that were planned to go into effect Jan. 1, and vowing to work out a new trade agreement by April. But with the details of that agreement still vague, farmers are not convinced they\u2019ll get back what was lost.</p>, <p>Even if the tariffs go away entirely, farmers and commodity leaders are unsure the U.S. will regain its share of the world market.</p>, <p>Kirk Merritt, executive director of the Ohio Soybean Association, told farmers at the annual Grain Farmer Symposium, Dec. 18, that he hopes they take advantage of the trade aid, and that he\u2019s optimistic the Chinese market will come back \u2014 but perhaps not as strong as before.</p>, <p>\u201cWe\u2019re optimistic that (talks) will lead to some renewal of that market, but I think it\u2019s probably safe to assume it\u2019s never going to be what it was,\u201d Merritt said.</p>, <p>Ultimately, the U.S. may need \u201cto build up additional markets to make up for what won\u2019t be there with China, even if China comes back,\u201d he added.</p>, <p>The U.S. has made progress on agreements with other nations, including South Korea, through a revised U.S. Korea Free Trade Agreement, and through a new agreement with Canada and Mexico, that replaced the North American Free Trade Agreement.</p>, <p>There is also strong interest in restoring trade with Japan, one of the key Pacific nations that was included in the Trans-Pacific partnership, which was negotiated before Trump took office, and which he pulled the U.S. away from in 2017.</p>, <p>Trump noted his angst for unfair trade policies during his campaign, arguing that China and other countries were taking advantage of the U.S. through poorly written free trade agreements. But the tariffs hit the wallets of one of his strongest campaign supporters \u2014 farmers and rural America.</p>, <p>Economists with Ohio State University estimated this summer that the tariffs could cost crop farmers more than half their income, if they continue, and that they\u2019ve already cost the U.S. most of its soybean exports to China, which last year bought more than $1.8 billion of Ohio soybeans alone.</p>, <p>While the situation has tested farmers\u2019 patience, and cost them money, many still say they support the president and believe his approach to trade will work in the end.</p>, <p>\u201cI think he\u2019s a decent president and I think in the end we will be OK, said Charles L. Kettering, an Ashland County farmer. \u201cI think all he\u2019s trying to do is make this country better.\u201d</p>, <p>David Eichelberger, also an Ashland County grain farmer, said he thinks the president is doing the right thing with trade, but the Chinese, in turn, \u201care hanging it over our heads.\u201d</p>, <p>He said the aid package will help, but at the same time, \u201cit\u2019s kind of a Band-Aid\u201d compared to what farmers are losing in the marketplace.</p>, <p>Katie Hill, the Farm Service Agency director in Knox County, said farmers have been trickling into the FSA office throughout the fall, as they finish harvest. She said it\u2019s important they keep the deadlines in mind, and keep good records of their yield, just as they should do for any FSA program.</p>, <p>Although the compensation differs widely among the commodities, Hill said soybean farmers are seeing some significant payments, because that crop is compensated the most.</p>, <p>\u201cAny addition they (farmers) can get this year is going to help them with the low commodity prices,\u201d Hill said.</p>, <p>The National Corn Growers Association has argued that the compensation to corn farmers should be higher, estimating that corn farmers lost 44 cents per bushel to tariffs, compared to the 1 cent compensation being offered.</p>, <p><strong>Related coverage:</strong></p>, <p><a href="https://www.farmers.gov/manage/mfp" onclick="javascript:_gaq.push(['_trackEvent','outbound-article','http://www.farmers.gov']);">\u2022 Second round of trade mitigation payments announced (Dec. 18, 2018)</a></p>, <p
